In this case, I don't mind being "that guy". With that said, this specific car has not been tested at 300+mph, the top speed of this car is unknown at this time.   As for the 300 mph "record" Bugatti broke, they have not broken any record, as of typing this the Koenigsegg Agera RS still retains the title.   The specific car Bugatti tested was not a production car in any manner, it was a test mule, which means it is disingenuous to claim "300 mph", but this applies to anyone who makes this claim.   IF Bugatti are handed this record by Guinness then the title will effectively be worthless and will be a repeat of the Veyron SS and the limiter they deprogrammed. Remember, customer cars weren't capable of the recorded 267 mph, they maxed out at 257  mph or so. IF it were possible to deprogram the limiter by Bugatti then it still wouldn't be a feature  present at time of production which means it would still not qualify for the record.   Feel free to present your arguments...

Matt getting far too excited by this mediocre demo. The 0-62mph (0-100kph) was 4 seconds -  not even close to a Tesla Model S P100D. The limited speed was only 188mph. And this car will almost never be able to run at 300mph. The conditions are too rarified. The Roadster 2 can hit 100kph no slower than 1.9 seconds. I also expect it to run at 500kph (312.5mph) in order to achieve the next benchmark that Elon Musk was alluding to (also impractical to achieve). Bugattis historically force themselves into a very temporary spotlight with brute force mechanics. More finessed vehicles always sit beside them. 15 years after it was made the McLaren F1 took on the then new Veyron and left it standing for most of a mile until the extra 15mph top end speed kicked in for the Veyron. It's an overhyped, over-rated car. It looks so ordinary next to a Rimac C2 and has notably less power and torque (Rimac = 1,888hp, 2,300nm, 0-100kph @ 1.85 seconds). Now THAT is a car to get excited about.

NARDÃ“ CIRCUIT.  The track is 12.5 kilometres (7.8Â mi) long[2]Â and is round, has four lanes for cars and motorcycles totaling 16 metres (52Â ft) in width and has a separate inner ring for trucks at a width of 9 metres (30Â ft). In the cars/motorcycle ring the lanes are banked at such a degree that a driver in the outer most lane doesn't need to turn the wheel while driving at speeds of up to 240Â km/h (149Â mph). In essence, at the so-called neutral speed which is different for the four lanes, one can drive as if in a straight lane. However extremely fast cars still require the steering wheel to be turned when going faster than the maximum neutral speed. For example theÂ Koenigsegg CCRÂ which set a speed record for a production car at the NardÃ² Ring did so with the steering wheel at a 30Â° angle. This speed record has since been beaten by theÂ Bugatti VeyronÂ at Volkswagen Group's privateÂ Ehra-LessienÂ straight line test track in Germany, and hence the CCR only holds the speed record for the NardÃ² Ring. In the process of fighting a turn as needed when going faster than the neutral speed quite a bit of potential top speed is lost and hence a fast car will go faster in a straight line than what is possible on the NardÃ³ Ring. Even at the neutral speed, in a banked turn a car runs a bit heavier than it would in a straight line, since the downforce created by the banking increases the rolling resistance on the tires. There has been one fatality at the ring. The neutral speed for the four car/motorcycle lanes are respectively:[3]  Lane 1 â€“ 100Â km/h (62Â mph)  Lane 2 â€“ 140Â km/h (87Â mph)  Lane 3 â€“ 190Â km/h (118Â mph)  Lane 4 â€“ 240Â km/h (149Â mph)  During regular weekly working activity the maximum speed allowed on the circular track is 240Â km/h (149Â mph). Higher speeds are only allowed at times when a client gets the track for its exclusive use. The neutral speed for the truck ring is between 80Â km/h (50Â mph) and 140Â km/h (87Â mph) over the width of the track, highest in the outer most part of the lane. The plant also includes other tracks; the most important is 6.222 km handling circuit, completely inside the circular one. It is characterized by a long main straight and sixteen curves of different radius and variable lateral slope. It can provide useful results for durability, reliability, vehicle dynamics and tire tests of both cars and motorbikes.[4] The track was featured in British TV seriesÂ Top GearÂ in 1992, showing footage of theÂ Jaguar XJ220, driven by Martin Brundle on a top speed test. It was again featured in the series 18 opener, whenÂ Jeremy Clarkson,Â Richard HammondÂ andÂ James MayÂ drove in aÂ Lamborghini Aventador, aÂ Noble M600Â and aÂ McLaren MP4-12C, respectively, to see who could reach the highest speed. The rough surface of the track figured prominently in the latter episode, and it was resurfaced shortly afterwards in 2018.[5]

LADIES AND GENTLEMEN: What Matt said in the beginning about the tyre cap's weight is completely correct. The tyre rotates at such speed when traveling at 300mph that it experiences some relativistic effects like increased weight. IN ADDITION, this car travels at 300mph; that is almost one third of the Earth's speed while turning. There is a small time dilation effect taking place which you can measure with a clock at the starting point synchronised to another clock on the Bugatti, but it's not nearly as pronounced when you're traveling at speeds of Mach 1 and higher. When you get into a Bugatti Chiron Super Sport, and travel at full speed, you jump the tiniest bit forward in spacetime.
